0 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003ePrior-preservation is used to avoid overfitting and language-drift. Refer to the paper to learn more about it. For prior-preservation we first generate images using the model with a class prompt and then use those during training along with our data.\nAccording to the paper, it's recommended to generate \u003ccode\u003enum_epochs * num_samples\u003c/code\u003e images for prior-preservation. 200-300 works well for most cases. The \u003ccode\u003enum_class_images\u003c/code\u003e flag sets the number of images to generate with the class prompt. You can place existing images in \u003ccode\u003eclass_data_dir\u003c/code\u003e, and the training script will generate any additional images so that \u003ccode\u003enum_class_images\u003c/code\u003e are present in \u003ccode\u003eclass_data_dir\u003c/code\u003e during training time.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" dir=\"auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"export MODEL_NAME=\u0026quot;CompVis/stable-diffusion-v1-4\u0026quot;\nexport INSTANCE_DIR=\u0026quot;dog\u0026quot;\nexport CLASS_DIR=\u0026quot;path-to-class-images\u0026quot;\nexport OUTPUT_DIR=\u0026quot;path-to-save-model\u0026quot;\n\naccelerate launch train_dreambooth.py \\\n  --pretrained_model_name_or_path=$MODEL_NAME  \\\n  --instance_data_dir=$INSTANCE_DIR \\\n  --class_data_dir=$CLASS_DIR \\\n  --output_dir=$OUTPUT_DIR \\\n  --with_prior_preservation --prior_loss_weight=1.0 \\\n  --instance_prompt=\u0026quot;a photo of sks dog\u0026quot; \\\n  --class_prompt=\u0026quot;a photo of dog\u0026quot; \\\n  --resolution=512 \\\n  --train_batch_size=1 \\\n  --gradient_accumulation_steps=1 \\\n  --learning_rate=5e-6 \\\n  --lr_scheduler=\u0026quot;constant\u0026quot; \\\n  --lr_warmup_steps=0 \\\n  --num_class_images=200 \\\n  --max_train_steps=800 \\\n  --push_to_hub\"\u003e\u003cpre\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003eexport\u003c/span\u003e MODEL_NAME=\u003cspan class=\"pl-s\"\u003e\u003cspan 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eBy using \u003ca href=\"https://www.deepspeed.ai/\" rel=\"nofollow\"\u003eDeepSpeed\u003c/a\u003e it's possible to offload some\ntensors from VRAM to either CPU or NVME allowing to train with less VRAM.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eDeepSpeed needs to be enabled with \u003ccode\u003eaccelerate config\u003c/code\u003e. During configuration\nanswer yes to \"Do you want to use DeepSpeed?\". With DeepSpeed stage 2, fp16\nmixed precision and offloading both parameters and optimizer state to cpu it's\npossible to train on under 8 GB VRAM with a drawback of requiring significantly\nmore RAM (about 25 GB). See \u003ca href=\"https://huggingface.co/docs/accelerate/usage_guides/deepspeed\" rel=\"nofollow\"\u003edocumentation\u003c/a\u003e for more DeepSpeed configuration options.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eChanging the default Adam optimizer to DeepSpeed's special version of Adam\n\u003ccode\u003edeepspeed.ops.adam.DeepSpeedCPUAdam\u003c/code\u003e gives a substantial speedup but enabling\nit requires CUDA toolchain with the same version as pytorch. 8-bit optimizer\ndoes not seem to be compatible with DeepSpeed at the moment.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"highlight The process is the same as above, all you need to do is replace the \u003ccode\u003eMODEL_NAME\u003c/code\u003e like this:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"export MODEL_NAME=\u0026quot;CompVis/stable-diffusion-v1-4\u0026quot; export MODEL_NAME=\"BAAI/AltDiffusion-m9\"\nor\nexport MODEL_NAME=\"CompVis/stable-diffusion-v1-4\" --\u0026gt; export MODEL_NAME=\"BAAI/AltDiffusion\"\n\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch3 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003eInference\u003c/h3\u003e\u003ca id=\"user-content-inference\" class=\"anchor\" aria-label=\"Permalink: Inference\" href=\"#inference\"\u003e\u003csvg class=\"octicon octicon-link\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003cpath d=\"m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eOnce you have trained a model using the above command, you can run inference simply using the \u003ccode\u003eStableDiffusionPipeline\u003c/code\u003e. Make sure to include the \u003ccode\u003eidentifier\u003c/code\u003e (e.g. sks in above example) in your prompt.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"highlight highlight-source-python notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" dir=\"auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"from diffusers import StableDiffusionPipeline\nimport torch\n\nmodel_id = dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch3 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003eInference from a training checkpoint\u003c/h3\u003e\u003ca id=\"user-content-inference-from-a-training-checkpoint\" class=\"anchor\" aria-label=\"Permalink: Inference from a training checkpoint\" href=\"#inference-from-a-training-checkpoint\"\u003e\u003csvg class=\"octicon octicon-link\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003cpath d=\"m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 from one of the checkpoints saved during the training process, if you used the \u003ccode\u003e--checkpointing_steps\u003c/code\u003e argument. Please, refer to \u003ca href=\"https://huggingface.co/docs/diffusers/main/en/training/dreambooth#performing-inference-using-a-saved-checkpoint\" rel=\"nofollow\"\u003ethe documentation\u003c/a\u003e to see how to do it.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch2 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003eTraining with Low-Rank Adaptation of Large Language Models (LoRA)\u003c/h2\u003e\u003ca id=\"user-content-training-with-low-rank-adaptation-of-large-language-models-lora\" class=\"anchor\" aria-label=\"Permalink: Training with Low-Rank Adaptation of Large Language Models (LoRA)\" href=\"#training-with-low-rank-adaptation-of-large-language-models-lora\"\u003e\u003csvg class=\"octicon octicon-link\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003cpath d=\"m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eLow-Rank Adaption of Large Language Models was first introduced by Microsoft in \u003ca href=\"https://huggingface.co/papers/2106.09685\" rel=\"nofollow\"\u003eLoRA: Low-Rank Adaptation of Large Language Models\u003c/a\u003e by \u003cem\u003eEdward J. Hu, Yelong Shen, Phillip Wallis, Zeyuan Allen-Zhu, Yuanzhi Li, Shean Wang, Lu Wang, Weizhu Chen\u003c/em\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eIn a nutshell, LoRA allows to adapt pretrained models by adding pairs of rank-decomposition matrices to existing weights and \u003cstrong\u003eonly\u003c/strong\u003e training those newly added weights. This has a couple of advantages:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cul dir=\"auto\"\u003e\n\u003cli\u003ePrevious pretrained weights are kept frozen so that the model is not prone to \u003ca href=\"https://www.pnas.org/doi/10.1073/pnas.1611835114\" rel=\"nofollow\"\u003ecatastrophic forgetting\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eRank-decomposition matrices have significantly fewer parameters than the original model, which means that trained LoRA weights are easily portable.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eLoRA attention layers allow to control to which extent the model is adapted towards new training images via a \u003ccode\u003escale\u003c/code\u003e parameter.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ul\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ca href=\"https://github.com/cloneofsimo\"\u003ecloneofsimo\u003c/a\u003e was the first to try out LoRA training for Stable Diffusion in\nthe popular \u003ca href=\"https://github.com/cloneofsimo/lora\"\u003elora\u003c/a\u003e GitHub repository.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch3 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003eTraining\u003c/h3\u003e\u003ca id=\"user-content-training\" class=\"anchor\" aria-label=\"Permalink: Training\" href=\"#training\"\u003e\u003csvg class=\"octicon octicon-link\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003cpath d=\"m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eLet's get started with a simple example. We will re-use the dog example of the \u003ca href=\"#dog-toy-example\"\u003eprevious section\u003c/a\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eFirst, you need to set-up your dreambooth training example as is explained in the \u003ca href=\"#Installing-the-dependencies\"\u003einstallation section\u003c/a\u003e.\nNext, let's download the dog dataset. Download images from \u003ca href=\"https://drive.google.com/drive/folders/1BO_dyz-p65qhBRRMRA4TbZ8qW4rB99JZ\" rel=\"nofollow\"\u003ehere\u003c/a\u003e and save them in a directory. Make sure to set \u003ccode\u003eINSTANCE_DIR\u003c/code\u003e to the name of your directory further below. This will be our training data.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eNow, you can launch the training. Here we will use \u003ca href=\"https://huggingface.co/stable-diffusion-v1-5/stable-diffusion-v1-5\" rel=\"nofollow\"\u003eStable Diffusion 1-5\u003c/a\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003e\u003cem\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eNote: Change the \u003ccode\u003eresolution\u003c/code\u003e to 768 if you are using the \u003ca href=\"https://huggingface.co/stabilityai/stable-diffusion-2\" rel=\"nofollow\"\u003estable-diffusion-2\u003c/a\u003e 768x768 model.\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/em\u003e\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003e\u003cem\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eNote: It is quite useful to monitor the training progress by regularly generating sample images during training. \u003ca href=\"https://docs.wandb.ai/quickstart\" rel=\"nofollow\"\u003ewandb\u003c/a\u003e is a nice solution to easily see generating images during training. All you need to do is to run \u003ccode\u003epip install wandb\u003c/code\u003e before training and pass \u003ccode\u003e--report_to=\"wandb\"\u003c/code\u003e to automatically log images.\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/em\u003e\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" dir=\"auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"export MODEL_NAME=\u0026quot;stable-diffusion-v1-5/stable-diffusion-v1-5\u0026quot;\nexport INSTANCE_DIR=\u0026quot;dog\u0026quot;\nexport OUTPUT_DIR=\u0026quot;path-to-save-model\u0026quot;\"\u003e\u003cpre\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003eexport\u003c/span\u003e MODEL_NAME=\u003cspan class=\"pl-s\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-pds\"\u003e\"\u003c/span\u003estable-diffusion-v1-5/stable-diffusion-v1-5\u003cspan class=\"pl-pds\"\u003e\"\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\n\u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003eexport\u003c/span\u003e INSTANCE_DIR=\u003cspan class=\"pl-s\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-pds\"\u003e\"\u003c/span\u003edog\u003cspan class=\"pl-pds\"\u003e\"\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\n\u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003eexport\u003c/span\u003e OUTPUT_DIR=\u003cspan class=\"pl-s\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-pds\"\u003e\"\u003c/span\u003epath-to-save-model\u003cspan class=\"pl-pds\"\u003e\"\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eFor this example we want to directly store the trained LoRA embeddings on the Hub, so\nwe need to be logged in and add the \u003ccode\u003e--push_to_hub\u003c/code\u003e flag.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" dir=\"auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"hf auth login\"\u003e\u003cpre\u003ehf auth login\u003c/pre\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eNow we can start training!\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" dir=\"auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"accelerate launch train_dreambooth_lora.py \\\n  --pretrained_model_name_or_path=$MODEL_NAME  \\\n  --instance_data_dir=$INSTANCE_DIR \\\n  --output_dir=$OUTPUT_DIR \\\n  --instance_prompt=\u0026quot;a photo of sks dog\u0026quot; \\\n  --resolution=512 \\\n  --train_batch_size=1 \\\n  --gradient_accumulation_steps=1 \\\n  --checkpointing_steps=100 \\\n  --learning_rate=1e-4 \\\n  --report_to=\u0026quot;wandb\u0026quot; \\\n  --lr_scheduler=\u0026quot;constant\u0026quot; \\\n  --lr_warmup_steps=0 \\\n  --max_train_steps=500 \\\n  --validation_prompt=\u0026quot;A photo of sks dog in a bucket\u0026quot; \\\n  --validation_epochs=50 \\\n  --seed=\u0026quot;0\u0026quot; \\\n  --push_to_hub\"\u003e\u003cpre\u003eaccelerate launch train_dreambooth_lora.py \\\n  --pretrained_model_name_or_path=\u003cspan class=\"pl-smi\"\u003e$MODEL_NAME\u003c/span\u003e  \\\n  --instance_data_dir=\u003cspan class=\"pl-smi\"\u003e$INSTANCE_DIR\u003c/span\u003e \\\n  --output_dir=\u003cspan class=\"pl-smi\"\u003e$OUTPUT_DIR\u003c/span\u003e \\\n  --instance_prompt=\u003cspan class=\"pl-s\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-pds\"\u003e\"\u003c/span\u003ea photo of sks dog\u003cspan class=\"pl-pds\"\u003e\"\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/span\u003e \\\n  --resolution=512 \\\n  --train_batch_size=1 \\\n  --gradient_accumulation_steps=1 \\\n  --checkpointing_steps=100 \\\n  --learning_rate=1e-4 \\\n  --report_to=\u003cspan class=\"pl-s\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-pds\"\u003e\"\u003c/span\u003ewandb\u003cspan class=\"pl-pds\"\u003e\"\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/span\u003e \\\n  --lr_scheduler=\u003cspan class=\"pl-s\"\u003e\u003cspan --validation_prompt=\u003cspan class=\"pl-s\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-pds\"\u003e\"\u003c/span\u003eA photo of sks dog in a bucket\u003cspan class=\"pl-pds\"\u003e\"\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/span\u003e \\\n  --push_to_hub\u003c/pre\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003e\u003cem\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eNote: When using LoRA we can use a much higher learning rate compared to vanilla dreambooth. Here we\nuse \u003cem\u003e1e-4\u003c/em\u003e instead of the usual \u003cem\u003e2e-6\u003c/em\u003e.\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/em\u003e\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eThe final LoRA embedding weights have been uploaded to \u003ca href=\"https://huggingface.co/patrickvonplaten/lora_dreambooth_dog_example\" rel=\"nofollow\"\u003epatrickvonplaten/lora_dreambooth_dog_example\u003c/a\u003e. \u003cstrong\u003e___Note: \u003ca href=\"https://huggingface.co/patrickvonplaten/lora/blob/main/pytorch_attn_procs.bin\" rel=\"nofollow\"\u003eThe final weights\u003c/a\u003e are only 3 MB in size which is orders of magnitudes smaller than the original model.\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eThe training results are summarized \u003ca href=\"https://api.wandb.ai/report/patrickvonplaten/xm6cd5q5\" rel=\"nofollow\"\u003ehere\u003c/a\u003e.\nYou can use the \u003ccode\u003eStep\u003c/code\u003e slider to see how the model learned the features of our subject while the model trained.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eOptionally, we can also train additional LoRA layers for the text encoder. Specify the \u003ccode\u003e--train_text_encoder\u003c/code\u003e argument above for that. If you're interested to know more about how we\nenable this support, check out this \u003ca href=\"https://github.com/huggingface/diffusers/pull/2918\" data-hovercard-type=\"pull_request\" data-hovercard-url=\"/huggingface/diffusers/pull/2918/hovercard\"\u003ePR\u003c/a\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eWith the default hyperparameters from the above, the training seems to go in a positive direction. Check out \u003ca href=\"https://wandb.ai/sayakpaul/dreambooth-lora/reports/test-23-04-17-17-00-13---Vmlldzo0MDkwNjMy\" rel=\"nofollow\"\u003ethis panel\u003c/a\u003e. The trained LoRA layers are available \u003ca href=\"https://huggingface.co/sayakpaul/dreambooth\" rel=\"nofollow\"\u003ehere\u003c/a\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch3 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003eInference\u003c/h3\u003e\u003ca id=\"user-content-inference-1\" class=\"anchor\" aria-label=\"Permalink: Inference\" href=\"#inference-1\"\u003e\u003csvg class=\"octicon octicon-link\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003cpath d=\"m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eAfter training, LoRA weights can be loaded very easily into the original pipeline. The full finetuning scripts will update the scheduler config for the full saved model. However, when loading saved LoRA weights, you\nmust also update the pipeline's scheduler config.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"highlight highlight-source-python notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" dir=\"auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"from diffusers import DiffusionPipeline\n\npipe = fixed variance schedule\npipe.scheduler = pipe.scheduler.__class__.from_config(pipe.scheduler.config, variance_type=\u0026quot;fixed_small\u0026quot;)\"\u003e\u003cpre\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-s\"\u003e\"fixed_small\"\u003c/span\u003e)\u003c/pre\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eAdditionally, a few alternative cli flags are needed for IF.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003e--resolution=64\u003c/code\u003e: IF is a pixel space diffusion model. In order to operate on un-compressed pixels, the input images are of a much smaller resolution.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003e--pre_compute_text_embeddings\u003c/code\u003e: IF uses \u003ca href=\"https://huggingface.co/docs/transformers/model_doc/t5\" rel=\"nofollow\"\u003eT5\u003c/a\u003e for its text encoder. In order to save GPU memory, we pre compute all text embeddings and then de-allocate\nT5.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003e--tokenizer_max_length=77\u003c/code\u003e: T5 has a longer default text length, but the default IF encoding procedure uses a smaller number.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003e--text_encoder_use_attention_mask\u003c/code\u003e: T5 passes the attention mask to the text encoder.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch3 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003eTips and Tricks\u003c/h3\u003e\u003ca id=\"user-content-tips-and-tricks\" class=\"anchor\" aria-label=\"Permalink: Tips and Tricks\" href=\"#tips-and-tricks\"\u003e\u003csvg class=\"octicon octicon-link\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003cpath d=\"m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eWe find LoRA to be sufficient for finetuning the stage I model as the low resolution of the model makes representing finegrained detail hard regardless.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eFor common and/or not-visually complex object concepts, you can get away with not-finetuning the upscaler. Just be sure to adjust the prompt passed to the\nupscaler to remove the new token from the instance prompt. I.e. if your stage I prompt is \"a sks dog\", use \"a dog\" for your stage II prompt.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eFor finegrained detail like faces that aren't present in the original training set, we find that full finetuning of the stage II upscaler is better than\nLoRA finetuning stage II.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eFor finegrained detail like faces, we find that lower learning rates along with larger batch sizes work best.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eFor stage II, we find that lower learning rates are also needed.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eWe found experimentally that the DDPM scheduler with the default larger number of denoising steps to sometimes work better than the DPM Solver scheduler\nused in the training scripts.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch3 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003eStage II additional validation images\u003c/h3\u003e\u003ca id=\"user-content-stage-ii-additional-validation-images\" class=\"anchor\" aria-label=\"Permalink: Stage II additional validation images\" Stage I Full Dreambooth\u003c/h3\u003e\u003ca id=\"user-content-if-stage-i-full-dreambooth\" class=\"anchor\" aria-label=\"Permalink: IF Stage I Full Dreambooth\" href=\"#if-stage-i-full-dreambooth\"\u003e\u003csvg class=\"octicon octicon-link\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003cpath d=\"m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003e--skip_save_text_encoder\u003c/code\u003e: When training the full model, this will skip saving the entire T5 with the finetuned model. You can still load the pipeline\nwith a T5 loaded from the original model.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003euse_8bit_adam\u003c/code\u003e: Due to the size of the optimizer states, we recommend training the full XL IF model with 8bit adam.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003e--learning_rate=1e-7\u003c/code\u003e: For full dreambooth, IF requires very low learning rates. With higher learning rates model quality will degrade. Note that it is\nlikely the learning rate can be increased with larger batch sizes.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eUsing 8bit adam and a batch size of 4, the model can be trained in ~48 GB VRAM.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003e--validation_scheduler\u003c/code\u003e: Set a particular scheduler via a string. We found that it is better to use the DDPMScheduler for validation when training DeepFloyd IF.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" dir=\"auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"export MODEL_NAME=\u0026quot;DeepFloyd/IF-I-XL-v1.0\u0026quot;\n\nexport INSTANCE_DIR=\u0026quot;dog\u0026quot;\nexport OUTPUT_DIR=\u0026quot;dreambooth_if\u0026quot;\n\naccelerate launch train_dreambooth.py \\\n  --pretrained_model_name_or_path=$MODEL_NAME  \\\n  --instance_data_dir=$INSTANCE_DIR \\\n  --output_dir=$OUTPUT_DIR \\\n  --instance_prompt=\u0026quot;a photo of sks dog\u0026quot; \\\n  --resolution=64 \\\n  --train_batch_size=4 \\\n  --gradient_accumulation_steps=1 \\\n DirectoryRichtextContent-module__SharedMarkdownContent__hHXUL" data-hpc="true"><article class="markdown-body entry-content container-lg" itemprop="text"><div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h1 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">DreamBooth training example</h1><a id="user-content-dreambooth-training-example" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: DreamBooth training example" href="#dreambooth-training-example"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto"><a href="https://huggingface.co/papers/2208.12242" rel="nofollow">DreamBooth</a> is a method to personalize text2image models like stable diffusion given just a few(3~5) images of a subject.
The <code>train_dreambooth.py</code> script shows how to implement the training procedure and adapt it for stable diffusion.</p>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h2 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Running locally with PyTorch</h2><a id="user-content-running-locally-with-pytorch" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Running locally with PyTorch" href="#running-locally-with-pytorch"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Installing the dependencies</h3><a id="user-content-installing-the-dependencies" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Installing the dependencies" href="#installing-the-dependencies"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">Before running the scripts, make sure to install the library's training dependencies:</p>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Important</strong></p>
<p dir="auto">To make sure you can successfully run the latest versions of the example scripts, we highly recommend <strong>installing from source</strong> and keeping the install up to date as we update the example scripts frequently and install some example-specific requirements. To do this, execute the following steps in a new virtual environment:</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="git clone https://github.com/huggingface/diffusers
cd diffusers
pip install -e ."><pre>git clone https://github.com/huggingface/diffusers
<span class="pl-c1">cd</span> diffusers
pip install -e <span class="pl-c1">.</span></pre></div>
<p dir="auto">Install the requirements in the <code>examples/dreambooth</code> folder as shown below.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="cd examples/dreambooth
pip install -r requirements.txt"><pre><span class="pl-c1">cd</span> examples/dreambooth
pip install -r requirements.txt</pre></div>
<p dir="auto">And initialize an <a href="https://github.com/huggingface/accelerate/">🤗Accelerate</a> environment with:</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="accelerate config"><pre>accelerate config</pre></div>
<p dir="auto">Or for a default accelerate configuration without answering questions about your environment</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="accelerate config default"><pre>accelerate config default</pre></div>
<p dir="auto">Or if your environment doesn't support an interactive shell e.g. a notebook</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-python notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="from accelerate.utils import write_basic_config
write_basic_config()"><pre><span class="pl-k">from</span> <span class="pl-s1">accelerate</span>.<span class="pl-s1">utils</span> <span class="pl-k">import</span> <span class="pl-s1">write_basic_config</span>
<span class="pl-en">write_basic_config</span>()</pre></div>
<p dir="auto">When running <code>accelerate config</code>, if we specify torch compile mode to True there can be dramatic speedups.
Note also that we use PEFT library as backend for LoRA training, make sure to have <code>peft&gt;=0.6.0</code> installed in your environment.</p>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Dog toy example</h3><a id="user-content-dog-toy-example" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Dog toy example" href="#dog-toy-example"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">Now let's get our dataset. For this example we will use some dog images: <a href="https://huggingface.co/datasets/diffusers/dog-example" rel="nofollow">https://huggingface.co/datasets/diffusers/dog-example</a>.</p>
<p dir="auto">Let's first download it locally:</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-python notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="from huggingface_hub import snapshot_download

local_dir = &quot;./dog&quot;
snapshot_download(
    &quot;diffusers/dog-example&quot;,
    local_dir=local_dir, repo_type=&quot;dataset&quot;,
    ignore_patterns=&quot;.gitattributes&quot;,
)"><pre><span class="pl-k">from</span> <span class="pl-s1">huggingface_hub</span> <span class="pl-k">import</span> <span class="pl-s1">snapshot_download</span>

<span class="pl-s1">local_dir</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-s">"./dog"</span>
<span class="pl-en">snapshot_download</span>(
    <span class="pl-s">"diffusers/dog-example"</span>,
    <span class="pl-s1">local_dir</span><span class="pl-c1">=</span><span class="pl-s1">local_dir</span>, <span class="pl-s1">repo_type</span><span class="pl-c1">=</span><span class="pl-s">"dataset"</span>,
    <span class="pl-s1">ignore_patterns</span><span class="pl-c1">=</span><span class="pl-s">".gitattributes"</span>,
)</pre></div>
<p dir="auto">And launch the training using:</p>
<p dir="auto"><strong><em><strong>Note: Change the <code>resolution</code> to 768 if you are using the <a href="https://huggingface.co/stabilityai/stable-diffusion-2" rel="nofollow">stable-diffusion-2</a> 768x768 model.</strong></em></strong></p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="export MODEL_NAME=&quot;CompVis/stable-diffusion-v1-4&quot;
export INSTANCE_DIR=&quot;dog&quot;
export OUTPUT_DIR=&quot;path-to-save-model&quot;

accelerate launch train_dreambooth.py \
  --pretrained_model_name_or_path=$MODEL_NAME  \
  --instance_data_dir=$INSTANCE_DIR \
  --output_dir=$OUTPUT_DIR \
  --instance_prompt=&quot;a photo of sks dog&quot; \
  --resolution=512 \
  --train_batch_size=1 \
  --gradient_accumulation_steps=1 \
  --learning_rate=5e-6 \
  --lr_scheduler=&quot;constant&quot; \
  --lr_warmup_steps=0 \
  --max_train_steps=400 \
  --push_to_hub"><pre><span class="pl-k">export</span> MODEL_NAME=<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>CompVis/stable-diffusion-v1-4<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span>
<span class="pl-k">export</span> INSTANCE_DIR=<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>dog<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span>
<span class="pl-k">export</span> OUTPUT_DIR=<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>path-to-save-model<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span>

accelerate launch train_dreambooth.py \
  --pretrained_model_name_or_path=<span class="pl-smi">$MODEL_NAME</span>  \
  --instance_data_dir=<span class="pl-smi">$INSTANCE_DIR</span> \
  --output_dir=<span class="pl-smi">$OUTPUT_DIR</span> \
  --instance_prompt=<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>a photo of sks dog<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span> \
  --resolution=512 \
  --train_batch_size=1 \
  --gradient_accumulation_steps=1 \
  --learning_rate=5e-6 \
  --lr_scheduler=<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>constant<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span> \
  --lr_warmup_steps=0 \
  --max_train_steps=400 \
  --push_to_hub</pre></div>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Training with prior-preservation loss</h3><a id="user-content-training-with-prior-preservation-loss" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Training with prior-preservation loss" href="#training-with-prior-preservation-loss"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">Prior-preservation is used to avoid overfitting and language-drift. Refer to the paper to learn more about it. For prior-preservation we first generate images using the model with a class prompt and then use those during training along with our data.
According to the paper, it's recommended to generate <code>num_epochs * num_samples</code> images for prior-preservation. 200-300 works well for most cases. The <code>num_class_images</code> flag sets the number of images to generate with the class prompt. You can place existing images in <code>class_data_dir</code>, and the training script will generate any additional images so that <code>num_class_images</code> are present in <code>class_data_dir</code> during training time.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="export MODEL_NAME=&quot;CompVis/stable-diffusion-v1-4&quot;
export INSTANCE_DIR=&quot;dog&quot;
export CLASS_DIR=&quot;path-to-class-images&quot;
export OUTPUT_DIR=&quot;path-to-save-model&quot;

accelerate launch train_dreambooth.py \
  --pretrained_model_name_or_path=$MODEL_NAME  \
  --instance_data_dir=$INSTANCE_DIR \
  --class_data_dir=$CLASS_DIR \
  --output_dir=$OUTPUT_DIR \
  --with_prior_preservation --prior_loss_weight=1.0 \
  --instance_prompt=&quot;a photo of sks dog&quot; \
  --class_prompt=&quot;a photo of dog&quot; \
  --resolution=512 \
  --train_batch_size=1 \
  --gradient_accumulation_steps=1 \
  --learning_rate=5e-6 \
  --lr_scheduler=&quot;constant&quot; \
  --lr_warmup_steps=0 \
  --num_class_images=200 \
  --max_train_steps=800 \
  --push_to_hub"><pre><span class="pl-k">export</span> MODEL_NAME=<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>CompVis/stable-diffusion-v1-4<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span>
<span class="pl-k">export</span> INSTANCE_DIR=<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>dog<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span>
<span class="pl-k">export</span> CLASS_DIR=<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>path-to-class-images<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span>
<span class="pl-k">export</span> OUTPUT_DIR=<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>path-to-save-model<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span>

accelerate launch train_dreambooth.py \
  --pretrained_model_name_or_path=<span class="pl-smi">$MODEL_NAME</span>  \
  --instance_data_dir=<span class="pl-smi">$INSTANCE_DIR</span> \
  --class_data_dir=<span class="pl-smi">$CLASS_DIR</span> \
  --output_dir=<span class="pl-smi">$OUTPUT_DIR</span> \
  --with_prior_preservation --prior_loss_weight=1.0 \
  --instance_prompt=<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>a photo of sks dog<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span> \
  --class_prompt=<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>a photo of dog<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span> \
  --resolution=512 \
  --train_batch_size=1 \
  --gradient_accumulation_steps=1 \
  --learning_rate=5e-6 \
  --lr_scheduler=<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>constant<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span> \
  --lr_warmup_steps=0 \
  --num_class_images=200 \
  --max_train_steps=800 \
  --push_to_hub</pre></div>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Training on a 16GB GPU:</h3><a id="user-content-training-on-a-16gb-gpu" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Training on a 16GB GPU:" href="#training-on-a-16gb-gpu"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">With the help of gradient checkpointing and the 8-bit optimizer from bitsandbytes it's possible to run train dreambooth on a 16GB GPU.</p>
<p dir="auto">To install <code>bitsandbytes</code> please refer to this <a href="https://github.com/TimDettmers/bitsandbytes#requirements--installation">readme</a>.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="export MODEL_NAME=&quot;CompVis/stable-diffusion-v1-4&quot;
export INSTANCE_DIR=&quot;dog&quot;
export CLASS_DIR=&quot;path-to-class-images&quot;
export OUTPUT_DIR=&quot;path-to-save-model&quot;

accelerate launch train_dreambooth.py \
  --pretrained_model_name_or_path=$MODEL_NAME  \
  --instance_data_dir=$INSTANCE_DIR \
  --class_data_dir=$CLASS_DIR \
  --output_dir=$OUTPUT_DIR \
  --with_prior_preservation --prior_loss_weight=1.0 \
  --instance_prompt=&quot;a photo of sks dog&quot; \
  --class_prompt=&quot;a photo of dog&quot; \
  --resolution=512 \
  --train_batch_size=1 \
  --gradient_accumulation_steps=2 --gradient_checkpointing \
  --use_8bit_adam \
  --learning_rate=5e-6 \
  --lr_scheduler=&quot;constant&quot; \
  --lr_warmup_steps=0 \
  --num_class_images=200 \
  --max_train_steps=800 \
  --push_to_hub"><pre><span class="pl-k">export</span> MODEL_NAME=<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>CompVis/stable-diffusion-v1-4<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span>
<span class="pl-k">export</span> INSTANCE_DIR=<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>dog<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span>
<span class="pl-k">export</span> CLASS_DIR=<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>path-to-class-images<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span>
<span class="pl-k">export</span> OUTPUT_DIR=<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>path-to-save-model<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span>

accelerate launch train_dreambooth.py \
  --pretrained_model_name_or_path=<span class="pl-smi">$MODEL_NAME</span>  \
  --instance_data_dir=<span class="pl-smi">$INSTANCE_DIR</span> \
  --class_data_dir=<span class="pl-smi">$CLASS_DIR</span> \
  --output_dir=<span class="pl-smi">$OUTPUT_DIR</span> \
  --with_prior_preservation --prior_loss_weight=1.0 \
  --instance_prompt=<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>a photo of sks dog<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span> \
  --class_prompt=<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>a photo of dog<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span> \
  --resolution=512 \
  --train_batch_size=1 \
  --gradient_accumulation_steps=2 --gradient_checkpointing \
  --use_8bit_adam \
  --learning_rate=5e-6 \
  --lr_scheduler=<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>constant<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span> \
  --lr_warmup_steps=0 \
  --num_class_images=200 \
  --max_train_steps=800 \
  --push_to_hub</pre></div>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Training on a 12GB GPU:</h3><a id="user-content-training-on-a-12gb-gpu" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Training on a 12GB GPU:" href="#training-on-a-12gb-gpu"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">It is possible to run dreambooth on a 12GB GPU by using the following optimizations:</p>
<ul dir="auto">
<li><a href="#training-on-a-16gb-gpu">gradient checkpointing and the 8-bit optimizer</a></li>
<li><a href="#training-with-xformers">xformers</a></li>
<li><a href="#set-grads-to-none">setting grads to none</a></li>
</ul>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="export MODEL_NAME=&quot;CompVis/stable-diffusion-v1-4&quot;
export INSTANCE_DIR=&quot;dog&quot;
export CLASS_DIR=&quot;path-to-class-images&quot;
export OUTPUT_DIR=&quot;path-to-save-model&quot;

accelerate launch train_dreambooth.py \
  --pretrained_model_name_or_path=$MODEL_NAME  \
  --instance_data_dir=$INSTANCE_DIR \
  --class_data_dir=$CLASS_DIR \
  --output_dir=$OUTPUT_DIR \
  --with_prior_preservation --prior_loss_weight=1.0 \
  --instance_prompt=&quot;a photo of sks dog&quot; \
  --class_prompt=&quot;a photo of dog&quot; \
  --resolution=512 \
  --train_batch_size=1 \
  --gradient_accumulation_steps=1 --gradient_checkpointing \
  --use_8bit_adam \
  --enable_xformers_memory_efficient_attention \
  --set_grads_to_none \
  --learning_rate=2e-6 \
  --lr_scheduler=&quot;constant&quot; \
  --lr_warmup_steps=0 \
  --num_class_images=200 \
  --max_train_steps=800 \
  --push_to_hub"><pre><span class="pl-k">export</span> MODEL_NAME=<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>CompVis/stable-diffusion-v1-4<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span>
<span class="pl-k">export</span> INSTANCE_DIR=<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>dog<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span>
<span class="pl-k">export</span> CLASS_DIR=<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>path-to-class-images<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span>
<span class="pl-k">export</span> OUTPUT_DIR=<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>path-to-save-model<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span>

accelerate launch train_dreambooth.py \
  --pretrained_model_name_or_path=<span class="pl-smi">$MODEL_NAME</span>  \
  --instance_data_dir=<span class="pl-smi">$INSTANCE_DIR</span> \
  --class_data_dir=<span class="pl-smi">$CLASS_DIR</span> \
  --output_dir=<span class="pl-smi">$OUTPUT_DIR</span> \

  --instance_prompt=<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>a photo of sks dog<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span> \
  --class_prompt=<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>a photo of dog<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span> \
  --resolution=512 \
  --train_batch_size=1 \
  --gradient_accumulation_steps=1 --gradient_checkpointing \
  --use_8bit_adam \
  --enable_xformers_memory_efficient_attention \
  --set_grads_to_none \
  --learning_rate=2e-6 \
  --lr_scheduler=<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>constant<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span> \
  --lr_warmup_steps=0 \
  --num_class_images=200 \
  --max_train_steps=800 \
  --push_to_hub</pre></div>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Training on a 8 GB GPU:</h3><a id="user-content-training-on-a-8-gb-gpu" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Training on a 8 GB GPU:" href="#training-on-a-8-gb-gpu"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">By using <a href="https://www.deepspeed.ai/" rel="nofollow">DeepSpeed</a> it's possible to offload some
tensors from VRAM to either CPU or NVME allowing to train with less VRAM.</p>
<p dir="auto">DeepSpeed needs to be enabled with <code>accelerate config</code>. During configuration
answer yes to "Do you want to use DeepSpeed?". With DeepSpeed stage 2, fp16
mixed precision and offloading both parameters and optimizer state to cpu it's
possible to train on under 8 GB VRAM with a drawback of requiring significantly
more RAM (about 25 GB). See <a href="https://huggingface.co/docs/accelerate/usage_guides/deepspeed" rel="nofollow">documentation</a> for more DeepSpeed configuration options.</p>
<p dir="auto">Changing the default Adam optimizer to DeepSpeed's special version of Adam
<code>deepspeed.ops.adam.DeepSpeedCPUAdam</code> gives a substantial speedup but enabling
it requires CUDA toolchain with the same version as pytorch. 8-bit optimizer
does not seem to be compatible with DeepSpeed at the moment.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="export MODEL_NAME=&quot;CompVis/stable-diffusion-v1-4&quot;
export INSTANCE_DIR=&quot;dog&quot;
export CLASS_DIR=&quot;path-to-class-images&quot;
export OUTPUT_DIR=&quot;path-to-save-model&quot;

accelerate launch --mixed_precision=&quot;fp16&quot; train_dreambooth.py \
  --pretrained_model_name_or_path=$MODEL_NAME \
  --instance_data_dir=$INSTANCE_DIR \
  --class_data_dir=$CLASS_DIR \
  --output_dir=$OUTPUT_DIR \
  --with_prior_preservation --prior_loss_weight=1.0 \
  --instance_prompt=&quot;a photo of sks dog&quot; \
  --class_prompt=&quot;a photo of dog&quot; \
  --resolution=512 \
  --train_batch_size=1 \
  --sample_batch_size=1 \
  --gradient_accumulation_steps=1 --gradient_checkpointing \
  --learning_rate=5e-6 \
  --lr_scheduler=&quot;constant&quot; \
  --lr_warmup_steps=0 \
  --num_class_images=200 \
  --max_train_steps=800 \
  --push_to_hub"><pre><span class="pl-k">export</span> MODEL_NAME=<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>CompVis/stable-diffusion-v1-4<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span>

accelerate launch --mixed_precision=<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>fp16<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span> train_dreambooth.py \

  --class_prompt=<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>a photo of dog<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span> \

  --train_batch_size=1 \
  --sample_batch_size=1 \

  --learning_rate=5e-6 \
  --lr_scheduler=<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>constant<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span> \
  --lr_warmup_steps=0 \
  --num_class_images=200 \
  --max_train_steps=800 \
  --push_to_hub</pre></div>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Fine-tune text encoder with the UNet.</h3><a id="user-content-fine-tune-text-encoder-with-the-unet" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Fine-tune text encoder with the UNet." href="#fine-tune-text-encoder-with-the-unet"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">The script also allows to fine-tune the <code>text_encoder</code> along with the <code>unet</code>. It's been observed experimentally that fine-tuning <code>text_encoder</code> gives much better results especially on faces.
Pass the <code>--train_text_encoder</code> argument to the script to enable training <code>text_encoder</code>.</p>
<p dir="auto"><em><strong>Note: Training text encoder requires more memory, with this option the training won't fit on 16GB GPU. It needs at least 24GB VRAM.</strong></em></p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="export MODEL_NAME=&quot;CompVis/stable-diffusion-v1-4&quot;
export INSTANCE_DIR=&quot;dog&quot;
export CLASS_DIR=&quot;path-to-class-images&quot;
export OUTPUT_DIR=&quot;path-to-save-model&quot;

accelerate launch train_dreambooth.py \
  --pretrained_model_name_or_path=$MODEL_NAME  \
  --train_text_encoder \
  --instance_data_dir=$INSTANCE_DIR \
  --class_data_dir=$CLASS_DIR \
  --output_dir=$OUTPUT_DIR \
  --with_prior_preservation --prior_loss_weight=1.0 \
  --instance_prompt=&quot;a photo of sks dog&quot; \
  --class_prompt=&quot;a photo of dog&quot; \
  --resolution=512 \
  --train_batch_size=1 \
  --use_8bit_adam \
  --gradient_checkpointing \
  --learning_rate=2e-6 \
  --lr_scheduler=&quot;constant&quot; \
  --lr_warmup_steps=0 \
  --num_class_images=200 \
  --max_train_steps=800 \
  --push_to_hub"><pre><span class="pl-k">export</span> MODEL_NAME=<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>CompVis/stable-diffusion-v1-4<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span>
<span class="pl-k">export</span> INSTANCE_DIR=<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>dog<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span>
<span class="pl-k">export</span> CLASS_DIR=<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>path-to-class-images<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span>
<span class="pl-k">export</span> OUTPUT_DIR=<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>path-to-save-model<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span>

accelerate launch train_dreambooth.py \
  --pretrained_model_name_or_path=<span class="pl-smi">$MODEL_NAME</span>  \
  --train_text_encoder \
  --instance_data_dir=<span class="pl-smi">$INSTANCE_DIR</span> \
  --class_data_dir=<span class="pl-smi">$CLASS_DIR</span> \
  --output_dir=<span class="pl-smi">$OUTPUT_DIR</span> \
  --with_prior_preservation --prior_loss_weight=1.0 \
  --instance_prompt=<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>a photo of sks dog<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span> \
  --class_prompt=<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>a photo of dog<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span> \
  --resolution=512 \
  --train_batch_size=1 \
  --use_8bit_adam \
  --gradient_checkpointing \
  --learning_rate=2e-6 \
  --lr_scheduler=<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>constant<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span> \
  --lr_warmup_steps=0 \
