  --max_train_steps=800 \
  --push_to_hub</pre></div>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Using DreamBooth for pipelines other than Stable Diffusion</h3><a id="user-content-using-dreambooth-for-pipelines-other-than-stable-diffusion" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Using DreamBooth for pipelines other than Stable Diffusion" href="#using-dreambooth-for-pipelines-other-than-stable-diffusion"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">The <a href="https://huggingface.co/docs/diffusers/api/pipelines/alt_diffusion" rel="nofollow">AltDiffusion pipeline</a> also supports dreambooth fine-tuning. The process is the same as above, all you need to do is replace the <code>MODEL_NAME</code> like this:</p>
<div class="snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="export MODEL_NAME=&quot;CompVis/stable-diffusion-v1-4&quot; --&gt; export MODEL_NAME=&quot;BAAI/AltDiffusion-m9&quot;
or
export MODEL_NAME=&quot;CompVis/stable-diffusion-v1-4&quot; --&gt; export MODEL_NAME=&quot;BAAI/AltDiffusion&quot;"><pre class="notranslate"><code>export MODEL_NAME="CompVis/stable-diffusion-v1-4" --&gt; export MODEL_NAME="BAAI/AltDiffusion-m9"
or
export MODEL_NAME="CompVis/stable-diffusion-v1-4" --&gt; export MODEL_NAME="BAAI/AltDiffusion"
</code></pre></div>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Inference</h3><a id="user-content-inference" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Inference" href="#inference"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">Once you have trained a model using the above command, you can run inference simply using the <code>StableDiffusionPipeline</code>. Make sure to include the <code>identifier</code> (e.g. sks in above example) in your prompt.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-python notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="from diffusers import StableDiffusionPipeline
import torch

model_id = &quot;path-to-your-trained-model&quot;
pipe = StableDiffusionPipeline.from_pretrained(model_id, torch_dtype=torch.float16).to(&quot;cuda&quot;)

prompt = &quot;A photo of sks dog in a bucket&quot;
image = pipe(prompt, num_inference_steps=50, guidance_scale=7.5).images[0]

image.save(&quot;dog-bucket.png&quot;)"><pre><span class="pl-k">from</span> <span class="pl-s1">diffusers</span> <span class="pl-k">import</span> <span class="pl-v">StableDiffusionPipeline</span>
<span class="pl-k">import</span> <span class="pl-s1">torch</span>

<span class="pl-s1">model_id</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-s">"path-to-your-trained-model"</span>
<span class="pl-s1">pipe</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-v">StableDiffusionPipeline</span>.<span class="pl-c1">from_pretrained</span>(<span class="pl-s1">model_id</span>, <span class="pl-s1">torch_dtype</span><span class="pl-c1">=</span><span class="pl-s1">torch</span>.<span class="pl-c1">float16</span>).<span class="pl-c1">to</span>(<span class="pl-s">"cuda"</span>)

<span class="pl-s1">prompt</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-s">"A photo of sks dog in a bucket"</span>
<span class="pl-s1">image</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-en">pipe</span>(<span class="pl-s1">prompt</span>, <span class="pl-s1">num_inference_steps</span><span class="pl-c1">=</span><span class="pl-c1">50</span>, <span class="pl-s1">guidance_scale</span><span class="pl-c1">=</span><span class="pl-c1">7.5</span>).<span class="pl-c1">images</span>[<span class="pl-c1">0</span>]

<span class="pl-s1">image</span>.<span class="pl-c1">save</span>(<span class="pl-s">"dog-bucket.png"</span>)</pre></div>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Inference from a training checkpoint</h3><a id="user-content-inference-from-a-training-checkpoint" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Inference from a training checkpoint" href="#inference-from-a-training-checkpoint"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">You can also perform inference from one of the checkpoints saved during the training process, if you used the <code>--checkpointing_steps</code> argument. Please, refer to <a href="https://huggingface.co/docs/diffusers/main/en/training/dreambooth#performing-inference-using-a-saved-checkpoint" rel="nofollow">the documentation</a> to see how to do it.</p>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h2 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Training with Low-Rank Adaptation of Large Language Models (LoRA)</h2><a id="user-content-training-with-low-rank-adaptation-of-large-language-models-lora" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Training with Low-Rank Adaptation of Large Language Models (LoRA)" href="#training-with-low-rank-adaptation-of-large-language-models-lora"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">Low-Rank Adaption of Large Language Models was first introduced by Microsoft in <a href="https://huggingface.co/papers/2106.09685" rel="nofollow">LoRA: Low-Rank Adaptation of Large Language Models</a> by <em>Edward J. Hu, Yelong Shen, Phillip Wallis, Zeyuan Allen-Zhu, Yuanzhi Li, Shean Wang, Lu Wang, Weizhu Chen</em></p>
<p dir="auto">In a nutshell, LoRA allows to adapt pretrained models by adding pairs of rank-decomposition matrices to existing weights and <strong>only</strong> training those newly added weights. This has a couple of advantages:</p>
<ul dir="auto">
<li>Previous pretrained weights are kept frozen so that the model is not prone to <a href="https://www.pnas.org/doi/10.1073/pnas.1611835114" rel="nofollow">catastrophic forgetting</a></li>
<li>Rank-decomposition matrices have significantly fewer parameters than the original model, which means that trained LoRA weights are easily portable.</li>
<li>LoRA attention layers allow to control to which extent the model is adapted towards new training images via a <code>scale</code> parameter.</li>
</ul>
<p dir="auto"><a href="https://github.com/cloneofsimo">cloneofsimo</a> was the first to try out LoRA training for Stable Diffusion in
the popular <a href="https://github.com/cloneofsimo/lora">lora</a> GitHub repository.</p>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Training</h3><a id="user-content-training" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Training" href="#training"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">Let's get started with a simple example. We will re-use the dog example of the <a href="#dog-toy-example">previous section</a>.</p>
<p dir="auto">First, you need to set-up your dreambooth training example as is explained in the <a href="#Installing-the-dependencies">installation section</a>.
Next, let's download the dog dataset. Download images from <a href="https://drive.google.com/drive/folders/1BO_dyz-p65qhBRRMRA4TbZ8qW4rB99JZ" rel="nofollow">here</a> and save them in a directory. Make sure to set <code>INSTANCE_DIR</code> to the name of your directory further below. This will be our training data.</p>
<p dir="auto">Now, you can launch the training. Here we will use <a href="https://huggingface.co/stable-diffusion-v1-5/stable-diffusion-v1-5" rel="nofollow">Stable Diffusion 1-5</a>.</p>
<p dir="auto"><strong><em><strong>Note: Change the <code>resolution</code> to 768 if you are using the <a href="https://huggingface.co/stabilityai/stable-diffusion-2" rel="nofollow">stable-diffusion-2</a> 768x768 model.</strong></em></strong></p>
<p dir="auto"><strong><em><strong>Note: It is quite useful to monitor the training progress by regularly generating sample images during training. <a href="https://docs.wandb.ai/quickstart" rel="nofollow">wandb</a> is a nice solution to easily see generating images during training. All you need to do is to run <code>pip install wandb</code> before training and pass <code>--report_to="wandb"</code> to automatically log images.</strong></em></strong></p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="export MODEL_NAME=&quot;stable-diffusion-v1-5/stable-diffusion-v1-5&quot;
export INSTANCE_DIR=&quot;dog&quot;
export OUTPUT_DIR=&quot;path-to-save-model&quot;"><pre><span class="pl-k">export</span> MODEL_NAME=<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>stable-diffusion-v1-5/stable-diffusion-v1-5<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span>
<span class="pl-k">export</span> INSTANCE_DIR=<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>dog<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span>
<span class="pl-k">export</span> OUTPUT_DIR=<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>path-to-save-model<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span></pre></div>
<p dir="auto">For this example we want to directly store the trained LoRA embeddings on the Hub, so
we need to be logged in and add the <code>--push_to_hub</code> flag.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="hf auth login"><pre>hf auth login</pre></div>
<p dir="auto">Now we can start training!</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="accelerate launch train_dreambooth_lora.py \
  --pretrained_model_name_or_path=$MODEL_NAME  \
  --instance_data_dir=$INSTANCE_DIR \
  --output_dir=$OUTPUT_DIR \
  --instance_prompt=&quot;a photo of sks dog&quot; \
  --resolution=512 \
  --train_batch_size=1 \
  --gradient_accumulation_steps=1 \
  --checkpointing_steps=100 \
  --learning_rate=1e-4 \
  --report_to=&quot;wandb&quot; \
  --lr_scheduler=&quot;constant&quot; \
  --lr_warmup_steps=0 \
  --max_train_steps=500 \
  --validation_prompt=&quot;A photo of sks dog in a bucket&quot; \
  --validation_epochs=50 \
  --seed=&quot;0&quot; \
  --push_to_hub"><pre>accelerate launch train_dreambooth_lora.py \
  --pretrained_model_name_or_path=<span class="pl-smi">$MODEL_NAME</span>  \
  --instance_data_dir=<span class="pl-smi">$INSTANCE_DIR</span> \
  --output_dir=<span class="pl-smi">$OUTPUT_DIR</span> \
  --instance_prompt=<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>a photo of sks dog<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span> \
  --resolution=512 \
  --train_batch_size=1 \
  --gradient_accumulation_steps=1 \
  --checkpointing_steps=100 \
  --learning_rate=1e-4 \
  --report_to=<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>wandb<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span> \
  --lr_scheduler=<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>constant<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span> \
  --lr_warmup_steps=0 \
  --max_train_steps=500 \
  --validation_prompt=<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>A photo of sks dog in a bucket<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span> \
  --validation_epochs=50 \
  --seed=<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>0<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span> \
  --push_to_hub</pre></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong><em><strong>Note: When using LoRA we can use a much higher learning rate compared to vanilla dreambooth. Here we
use <em>1e-4</em> instead of the usual <em>2e-6</em>.</strong></em></strong></p>
<p dir="auto">The final LoRA embedding weights have been uploaded to <a href="https://huggingface.co/patrickvonplaten/lora_dreambooth_dog_example" rel="nofollow">patrickvonplaten/lora_dreambooth_dog_example</a>. <strong>___Note: <a href="https://huggingface.co/patrickvonplaten/lora/blob/main/pytorch_attn_procs.bin" rel="nofollow">The final weights</a> are only 3 MB in size which is orders of magnitudes smaller than the original model.</strong></p>
<p dir="auto">The training results are summarized <a href="https://api.wandb.ai/report/patrickvonplaten/xm6cd5q5" rel="nofollow">here</a>.
You can use the <code>Step</code> slider to see how the model learned the features of our subject while the model trained.</p>
<p dir="auto">Optionally, we can also train additional LoRA layers for the text encoder. Specify the <code>--train_text_encoder</code> argument above for that. If you're interested to know more about how we
enable this support, check out this <a href="https://github.com/huggingface/diffusers/pull/2918" data-hovercard-type="pull_request" data-hovercard-url="/huggingface/diffusers/pull/2918/hovercard">PR</a>.</p>
<p dir="auto">With the default hyperparameters from the above, the training seems to go in a positive direction. Check out <a href="https://wandb.ai/sayakpaul/dreambooth-lora/reports/test-23-04-17-17-00-13---Vmlldzo0MDkwNjMy" rel="nofollow">this panel</a>. The trained LoRA layers are available <a href="https://huggingface.co/sayakpaul/dreambooth" rel="nofollow">here</a>.</p>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Inference</h3><a id="user-content-inference-1" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Inference" href="#inference-1"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">After training, LoRA weights can be loaded very easily into the original pipeline. First, you need to
load the original pipeline:</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-python notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="from diffusers import DiffusionPipeline
pipe = DiffusionPipeline.from_pretrained(&quot;base-model-name&quot;).to(&quot;cuda&quot;)"><pre><span class="pl-k">from</span> <span class="pl-s1">diffusers</span> <span class="pl-k">import</span> <span class="pl-v">DiffusionPipeline</span>
<span class="pl-s1">pipe</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-v">DiffusionPipeline</span>.<span class="pl-c1">from_pretrained</span>(<span class="pl-s">"base-model-name"</span>).<span class="pl-c1">to</span>(<span class="pl-s">"cuda"</span>)</pre></div>
<p dir="auto">Next, we can load the adapter layers into the pipeline with the <a href="https://huggingface.co/docs/diffusers/main/en/using-diffusers/loading_adapters#lora" rel="nofollow"><code>load_lora_weights</code> function</a>.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-python notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="pipe.load_lora_weights(&quot;path-to-the-lora-checkpoint&quot;)"><pre><span class="pl-s1">pipe</span>.<span class="pl-c1">load_lora_weights</span>(<span class="pl-s">"path-to-the-lora-checkpoint"</span>)</pre></div>
<p dir="auto">Finally, we can run the model in inference.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-python notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="image = pipe(&quot;A picture of a sks dog in a bucket&quot;, num_inference_steps=25).images[0]"><pre><span class="pl-s1">image</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-en">pipe</span>(<span class="pl-s">"A picture of a sks dog in a bucket"</span>, <span class="pl-s1">num_inference_steps</span><span class="pl-c1">=</span><span class="pl-c1">25</span>).<span class="pl-c1">images</span>[<span class="pl-c1">0</span>]</pre></div>
<p dir="auto">If you are loading the LoRA parameters from the Hub and if the Hub repository has
a <code>base_model</code> tag (such as <a href="https://huggingface.co/patrickvonplaten/lora_dreambooth_dog_example/blob/main/README.md?code=true#L4" rel="nofollow">this</a>), then
you can do:</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-python notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="from huggingface_hub.repocard import RepoCard

lora_model_id = &quot;patrickvonplaten/lora_dreambooth_dog_example&quot;
card = RepoCard.load(lora_model_id)
base_model_id = card.data.to_dict()[&quot;base_model&quot;]

pipe = StableDiffusionPipeline.from_pretrained(base_model_id, torch_dtype=torch.float16)
..."><pre><span class="pl-k">from</span> <span class="pl-s1">huggingface_hub</span>.<span class="pl-s1">repocard</span> <span class="pl-k">import</span> <span class="pl-v">RepoCard</span>

<span class="pl-s1">lora_model_id</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-s">"patrickvonplaten/lora_dreambooth_dog_example"</span>
<span class="pl-s1">card</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-v">RepoCard</span>.<span class="pl-c1">load</span>(<span class="pl-s1">lora_model_id</span>)
<span class="pl-s1">base_model_id</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-s1">card</span>.<span class="pl-c1">data</span>.<span class="pl-c1">to_dict</span>()[<span class="pl-s">"base_model"</span>]

<span class="pl-s1">pipe</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-v">StableDiffusionPipeline</span>.<span class="pl-c1">from_pretrained</span>(<span class="pl-s1">base_model_id</span>, <span class="pl-s1">torch_dtype</span><span class="pl-c1">=</span><span class="pl-s1">torch</span>.<span class="pl-c1">float16</span>)
...</pre></div>
<p dir="auto">If you used <code>--train_text_encoder</code> during training, then use <code>pipe.load_lora_weights()</code> to load the LoRA
weights. For example:</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-python notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="from huggingface_hub.repocard import RepoCard
from diffusers import StableDiffusionPipeline
import torch

lora_model_id = &quot;sayakpaul/dreambooth-text-encoder-test&quot;
card = RepoCard.load(lora_model_id)
base_model_id = card.data.to_dict()[&quot;base_model&quot;]

pipe = StableDiffusionPipeline.from_pretrained(base_model_id, torch_dtype=torch.float16)
pipe = pipe.to(&quot;cuda&quot;)
pipe.load_lora_weights(lora_model_id)
image = pipe(&quot;A picture of a sks dog in a bucket&quot;, num_inference_steps=25).images[0]"><pre><span class="pl-k">from</span> <span class="pl-s1">huggingface_hub</span>.<span class="pl-s1">repocard</span> <span class="pl-k">import</span> <span class="pl-v">RepoCard</span>
<span class="pl-k">from</span> <span class="pl-s1">diffusers</span> <span class="pl-k">import</span> <span class="pl-v">StableDiffusionPipeline</span>
<span class="pl-k">import</span> <span class="pl-s1">torch</span>

<span class="pl-s1">lora_model_id</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-s">"sayakpaul/dreambooth-text-encoder-test"</span>
<span class="pl-s1">card</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-v">RepoCard</span>.<span class="pl-c1">load</span>(<span class="pl-s1">lora_model_id</span>)
<span class="pl-s1">base_model_id</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-s1">card</span>.<span class="pl-c1">data</span>.<span class="pl-c1">to_dict</span>()[<span class="pl-s">"base_model"</span>]

<span class="pl-s1">pipe</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-v">StableDiffusionPipeline</span>.<span class="pl-c1">from_pretrained</span>(<span class="pl-s1">base_model_id</span>, <span class="pl-s1">torch_dtype</span><span class="pl-c1">=</span><span class="pl-s1">torch</span>.<span class="pl-c1">float16</span>)
<span class="pl-s1">pipe</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-s1">pipe</span>.<span class="pl-c1">to</span>(<span class="pl-s">"cuda"</span>)
<span class="pl-s1">pipe</span>.<span class="pl-c1">load_lora_weights</span>(<span class="pl-s1">lora_model_id</span>)
<span class="pl-s1">image</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-en">pipe</span>(<span class="pl-s">"A picture of a sks dog in a bucket"</span>, <span class="pl-s1">num_inference_steps</span><span class="pl-c1">=</span><span class="pl-c1">25</span>).<span class="pl-c1">images</span>[<span class="pl-c1">0</span>]</pre></div>
<p dir="auto">Note that the use of <a href="https://huggingface.co/docs/diffusers/main/en/api/loaders#diffusers.loaders.StableDiffusionLoraLoaderMixin.load_lora_weights" rel="nofollow"><code>StableDiffusionLoraLoaderMixin.load_lora_weights</code></a> is preferred to <a href="https://huggingface.co/docs/diffusers/main/en/api/loaders#diffusers.loaders.UNet2DConditionLoadersMixin.load_attn_procs" rel="nofollow"><code>UNet2DConditionLoadersMixin.load_attn_procs</code></a> for loading LoRA parameters. This is because
<code>StableDiffusionLoraLoaderMixin.load_lora_weights</code> can handle the following situations:</p>
<ul dir="auto">
<li>
<p dir="auto">LoRA parameters that don't have separate identifiers for the UNet and the text encoder (such as <a href="https://huggingface.co/patrickvonplaten/lora_dreambooth_dog_example" rel="nofollow"><code>"patrickvonplaten/lora_dreambooth_dog_example"</code></a>). So, you can just do:</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-python notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="pipe.load_lora_weights(lora_model_path)"><pre><span class="pl-s1">pipe</span>.<span class="pl-c1">load_lora_weights</span>(<span class="pl-s1">lora_model_path</span>)</pre></div>
</li>
<li>
<p dir="auto">LoRA parameters that have separate identifiers for the UNet and the text encoder such as: <a href="https://huggingface.co/sayakpaul/dreambooth" rel="nofollow"><code>"sayakpaul/dreambooth"</code></a>.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h2 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Training with Flax/JAX</h2><a id="user-content-training-with-flaxjax" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Training with Flax/JAX" href="#training-with-flaxjax"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">For faster training on TPUs and GPUs you can leverage the flax training example. Follow the instructions above to get the model and dataset before running the script.</p>
<p dir="auto">_<em><strong>Note: The flax example don't yet support features like gradient checkpoint, gradient accumulation etc, so to use flax for faster training we will need &gt;30GB cards.</strong></em></p>
<p dir="auto">Before running the scripts, make sure to install the library's training dependencies:</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="pip install -U -r requirements_flax.txt"><pre>pip install -U -r requirements_flax.txt</pre></div>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Training without prior preservation loss</h3><a id="user-content-training-without-prior-preservation-loss" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Training without prior preservation loss" href="#training-without-prior-preservation-loss"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>

<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Training with prior preservation loss</h3><a id="user-content-training-with-prior-preservation-loss-1" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Training with prior preservation loss" href="#training-with-prior-preservation-loss-1"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="export MODEL_NAME=&quot;duongna/stable-diffusion-v1-4-flax&quot;

<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Fine-tune text encoder with the UNet.</h3><a id="user-content-fine-tune-text-encoder-with-the-unet-1" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Fine-tune text encoder with the UNet." href="#fine-tune-text-encoder-with-the-unet-1"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>

<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Training with xformers:</h3><a id="user-content-training-with-xformers" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Training with xformers:" href="#training-with-xformers"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">You can enable memory efficient attention by <a href="https://github.com/facebookresearch/xformers#installing-xformers">installing xFormers</a> and padding the <code>--enable_xformers_memory_efficient_attention</code> argument to the script. This is not available with the Flax/JAX implementation.</p>
<p dir="auto">You can also use Dreambooth to train the specialized in-painting model. See <a href="https://github.com/huggingface/diffusers/tree/main/examples/research_projects/dreambooth_inpaint">the script in the research folder for details</a>.</p>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Set grads to none</h3><a id="user-content-set-grads-to-none" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Set grads to none" href="#set-grads-to-none"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">To save even more memory, pass the <code>--set_grads_to_none</code> argument to the script. This will set grads to None instead of zero. However, be aware that it changes certain behaviors, so if you start experiencing any problems, remove this argument.</p>
<p dir="auto">More info: <a href="https://pytorch.org/docs/stable/generated/torch.optim.Optimizer.zero_grad.html" rel="nofollow">https://pytorch.org/docs/stable/generated/torch.optim.Optimizer.zero_grad.html</a></p>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Experimental results</h3><a id="user-content-experimental-results" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Experimental results" href="#experimental-results"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">You can refer to <a href="https://huggingface.co/blog/dreambooth" rel="nofollow">this blog post</a> that discusses some of DreamBooth experiments in detail. Specifically, it recommends a set of DreamBooth-specific tips and tricks that we have found to work well for a variety of subjects.</p>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h2 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">IF</h2><a id="user-content-if" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: IF" href="#if"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">You can use the lora and full dreambooth scripts to train the text to image <a href="https://huggingface.co/DeepFloyd/IF-I-XL-v1.0" rel="nofollow">IF model</a> and the stage II upscaler
<a href="https://huggingface.co/DeepFloyd/IF-II-L-v1.0" rel="nofollow">IF model</a>.</p>
<p dir="auto">Note that IF has a predicted variance, and our finetuning scripts only train the models predicted error, so for finetuned IF models we switch to a fixed
variance schedule. The full finetuning scripts will update the scheduler config for the full saved model. However, when loading saved LoRA weights, you
must also update the pipeline's scheduler config.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-python notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="from diffusers import DiffusionPipeline

pipe = DiffusionPipeline.from_pretrained(&quot;DeepFloyd/IF-I-XL-v1.0&quot;)

pipe.load_lora_weights(&quot;&lt;lora weights path&gt;&quot;)

# Update scheduler config to fixed variance schedule
pipe.scheduler = pipe.scheduler.__class__.from_config(pipe.scheduler.config, variance_type=&quot;fixed_small&quot;)"><pre><span class="pl-k">from</span> <span class="pl-s1">diffusers</span> <span class="pl-k">import</span> <span class="pl-v">DiffusionPipeline</span>

<span class="pl-s1">pipe</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-v">DiffusionPipeline</span>.<span class="pl-c1">from_pretrained</span>(<span class="pl-s">"DeepFloyd/IF-I-XL-v1.0"</span>)

<span class="pl-s1">pipe</span>.<span class="pl-c1">load_lora_weights</span>(<span class="pl-s">"&lt;lora weights path&gt;"</span>)

<span class="pl-c"># Update scheduler config to fixed variance schedule</span>
<span class="pl-s1">pipe</span>.<span class="pl-c1">scheduler</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-s1">pipe</span>.<span class="pl-c1">scheduler</span>.<span class="pl-c1">__class__</span>.<span class="pl-c1">from_config</span>(<span class="pl-s1">pipe</span>.<span class="pl-c1">scheduler</span>.<span class="pl-c1">config</span>, <span class="pl-s1">variance_type</span><span class="pl-c1">=</span><span class="pl-s">"fixed_small"</span>)</pre></div>
<p dir="auto">Additionally, a few alternative cli flags are needed for IF.</p>
<p dir="auto"><code>--resolution=64</code>: IF is a pixel space diffusion model. In order to operate on un-compressed pixels, the input images are of a much smaller resolution.</p>
<p dir="auto"><code>--pre_compute_text_embeddings</code>: IF uses <a href="https://huggingface.co/docs/transformers/model_doc/t5" rel="nofollow">T5</a> for its text encoder. In order to save GPU memory, we pre compute all text embeddings and then de-allocate
T5.</p>
<p dir="auto"><code>--tokenizer_max_length=77</code>: T5 has a longer default text length, but the default IF encoding procedure uses a smaller number.</p>
<p dir="auto"><code>--text_encoder_use_attention_mask</code>: T5 passes the attention mask to the text encoder.</p>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Tips and Tricks</h3><a id="user-content-tips-and-tricks" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Tips and Tricks" href="#tips-and-tricks"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">We find LoRA to be sufficient for finetuning the stage I model as the low resolution of the model makes representing finegrained detail hard regardless.</p>
<p dir="auto">For common and/or not-visually complex object concepts, you can get away with not-finetuning the upscaler. Just be sure to adjust the prompt passed to the
upscaler to remove the new token from the instance prompt. I.e. if your stage I prompt is "a sks dog", use "a dog" for your stage II prompt.</p>
<p dir="auto">For finegrained detail like faces that aren't present in the original training set, we find that full finetuning of the stage II upscaler is better than
LoRA finetuning stage II.</p>
<p dir="auto">For finegrained detail like faces, we find that lower learning rates along with larger batch sizes work best.</p>
<p dir="auto">For stage II, we find that lower learning rates are also needed.</p>
<p dir="auto">We found experimentally that the DDPM scheduler with the default larger number of denoising steps to sometimes work better than the DPM Solver scheduler
used in the training scripts.</p>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Stage II additional validation images</h3><a id="user-content-stage-ii-additional-validation-images" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Stage II additional validation images" href="#stage-ii-additional-validation-images"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">The stage II validation requires images to upscale, we can download a downsized version of the training set:</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-python notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="from huggingface_hub import snapshot_download

    &quot;diffusers/dog-example-downsized&quot;,
    local_dir=local_dir,
    repo_type=&quot;dataset&quot;,
    ignore_patterns=&quot;.gitattributes&quot;,
)"><pre><span class="pl-k">from</span> <span class="pl-s1">huggingface_hub</span> <span class="pl-k">import</span> <span class="pl-s1">snapshot_download</span>

<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">IF stage I LoRA Dreambooth</h3><a id="user-content-if-stage-i-lora-dreambooth" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: IF stage I LoRA Dreambooth" href="#if-stage-i-lora-dreambooth"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">This training configuration requires ~28 GB VRAM.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="export MODEL_NAME=&quot;DeepFloyd/IF-I-XL-v1.0&quot;

<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">IF stage II LoRA Dreambooth</h3><a id="user-content-if-stage-ii-lora-dreambooth" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: IF stage II LoRA Dreambooth" href="#if-stage-ii-lora-dreambooth"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto"><code>--validation_images</code>: These images are upscaled during validation steps.</p>
<p dir="auto"><code>--class_labels_conditioning=timesteps</code>: Pass additional conditioning to the UNet needed for stage II.</p>
<p dir="auto"><code>--learning_rate=1e-6</code>: Lower learning rate than stage I.</p>
<p dir="auto"><code>--resolution=256</code>: The upscaler expects higher resolution inputs</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="export MODEL_NAME=&quot;DeepFloyd/IF-II-L-v1.0&quot;

<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">IF Stage I Full Dreambooth</h3><a id="user-content-if-stage-i-full-dreambooth" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: IF Stage I Full Dreambooth" href="#if-stage-i-full-dreambooth"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto"><code>--skip_save_text_encoder</code>: When training the full model, this will skip saving the entire T5 with the finetuned model. You can still load the pipeline
with a T5 loaded from the original model.</p>
<p dir="auto"><code>use_8bit_adam</code>: Due to the size of the optimizer states, we recommend training the full XL IF model with 8bit adam.</p>
<p dir="auto"><code>--learning_rate=1e-7</code>: For full dreambooth, IF requires very low learning rates. With higher learning rates model quality will degrade. Note that it is
likely the learning rate can be increased with larger batch sizes.</p>
<p dir="auto">Using 8bit adam and a batch size of 4, the model can be trained in ~48 GB VRAM.</p>
<p dir="auto"><code>--validation_scheduler</code>: Set a particular scheduler via a string. We found that it is better to use the DDPMScheduler for validation when training DeepFloyd IF.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="export MODEL_NAME=&quot;DeepFloyd/IF-I-XL-v1.0&quot;

export INSTANCE_DIR=&quot;dog&quot;
export OUTPUT_DIR=&quot;dreambooth_if&quot;

accelerate launch train_dreambooth.py \
  --pretrained_model_name_or_path=$MODEL_NAME  \
  --instance_data_dir=$INSTANCE_DIR \
  --output_dir=$OUTPUT_DIR \
  --instance_prompt=&quot;a photo of sks dog&quot; \
  --resolution=64 \
  --train_batch_size=4 \
  --gradient_accumulation_steps=1 \
  --learning_rate=1e-7 \
  --max_train_steps=150 \
  --validation_prompt &quot;a photo of sks dog&quot; \
  --validation_steps 25 \
  --text_encoder_use_attention_mask \
  --tokenizer_max_length 77 \
  --pre_compute_text_embeddings \
  --use_8bit_adam \
  --set_grads_to_none \
  --skip_save_text_encoder \
  --validation_scheduler DDPMScheduler \
  --push_to_hub"><pre><span class="pl-k">export</span> MODEL_NAME=<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>DeepFloyd/IF-I-XL-v1.0<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span>

<span class="pl-k">export</span> OUTPUT_DIR=<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>dreambooth_if<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span>

accelerate launch train_dreambooth.py \
  --pretrained_model_name_or_path=<span class="pl-smi">$MODEL_NAME</span>  \
  --instance_data_dir=<span class="pl-smi">$INSTANCE_DIR</span> \
  --output_dir=<span class="pl-smi">$OUTPUT_DIR</span> \
  --instance_prompt=<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>a photo of sks dog<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span> \
  --resolution=64 \
  --train_batch_size=4 \
  --gradient_accumulation_steps=1 \
  --learning_rate=1e-7 \
  --max_train_steps=150 \
  --validation_prompt <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>a photo of sks dog<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span> \
  --validation_steps 25 \
  --text_encoder_use_attention_mask \
  --tokenizer_max_length 77 \
  --pre_compute_text_embeddings \
  --use_8bit_adam \
  --set_grads_to_none \
  --skip_save_text_encoder \
  --validation_scheduler DDPMScheduler \
  --push_to_hub</pre></div>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">IF Stage II Full Dreambooth</h3><a id="user-content-if-stage-ii-full-dreambooth" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: IF Stage II Full Dreambooth" href="#if-stage-ii-full-dreambooth"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto"><code>--learning_rate=5e-6</code>: With a smaller effective batch size of 4, we found that we required learning rates as low as
1e-8.</p>
<p dir="auto"><code>--resolution=256</code>: The upscaler expects higher resolution inputs</p>
<p dir="auto"><code>--train_batch_size=2</code> and <code>--gradient_accumulation_steps=6</code>: We found that full training of stage II particularly with
faces required large effective batch sizes.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="export MODEL_NAME=&quot;DeepFloyd/IF-II-L-v1.0&quot;

<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h2 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Stable Diffusion XL</h2><a id="user-content-stable-diffusion-xl" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Stable Diffusion XL" href="#stable-diffusion-xl"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">We support fine-tuning of the UNet shipped in <a href="https://huggingface.co/papers/2307.01952" rel="nofollow">Stable Diffusion XL</a> with DreamBooth and LoRA via the <code>train_dreambooth_lora_sdxl.py</code> script. Please refer to the docs <a href="/huggingface/diffusers/blob/main/examples/dreambooth/README_sdxl.md">here</a>.</p>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h2 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Dataset</h2><a id="user-content-dataset" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Dataset" href="#dataset"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">We support 🤗 <a href="https://huggingface.co/docs/datasets/index" rel="nofollow">Datasets</a>, you can find a dataset on the <a href="https://huggingface.co/datasets" rel="nofollow">Hugging Face Hub</a> or use your own.</p>
<p dir="auto">The quickest way to get started with your custom dataset is 🤗 Datasets' <a href="https://huggingface.co/docs/datasets/image_dataset#imagefolder" rel="nofollow"><code>ImageFolder</code></a>.</p>
<p dir="auto">We need to create a file <code>metadata.jsonl</code> in the directory with our images:</p>
<div class="snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="{&quot;file_name&quot;: &quot;01.jpg&quot;, &quot;prompt&quot;: &quot;prompt 01&quot;}
{&quot;file_name&quot;: &quot;02.jpg&quot;, &quot;prompt&quot;: &quot;prompt 02&quot;}"><pre class="notranslate"><code>{"file_name": "01.jpg", "prompt": "prompt 01"}
{"file_name": "02.jpg", "prompt": "prompt 02"}
</code></pre></div>
<p dir="auto">If we have a directory with image-text pairs e.g. <code>01.jpg</code> and <code>01.txt</code> then <code>convert_to_imagefolder.py</code> can create <code>metadata.jsonl</code>.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="python convert_to_imagefolder.py --path my_dataset/"><pre>python convert_to_imagefolder.py --path my_dataset/</pre></div>
<p dir="auto">We use <code>--dataset_name</code> and <code>--caption_column</code> with training scripts.</p>
<div class="snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="--dataset_name=my_dataset/
--caption_column=prompt"><pre class="notranslate"><code>--dataset_name=my_dataset/
--caption_column=prompt
</code></pre></div>
</article></div></div></div></div></div></div></div></div></div></div></div><div class="ScrollMarksContainer-module__scrollMarksContainer__Eu7uU" id="find-result-marks-container"></div><button hidden="" data-testid="" data-hotkey-scope="read-only-cursor-text-area"></button><button hidden=""></button></div> <!-- --> <!-- --> <script type="application/json" id="__PRIMER_DATA__R_1___">{"resolvedServerColorMode":"day"}</script></div>
</react-app>




  </div>

</turbo-frame>

    </main>
  </div>

  </div>
